         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405288-sec-0080">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202405288-sec-0080-title">2.6 Charge-Storage Kinetics Analysis for C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> Anode</h3>
            
            <p>To investigate the charge transfer kinetics of C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> and MoSe<sub>2</sub> electrodes, we employed in situ galvanostatic electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (GEIS). As depicted in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0005">5a</a>, the semicircular impedance for C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> electrode consistently decreased from the open-circuit voltage (OCV) to 0.01&nbsp;V. It was noted that the impedance at 0.01&nbsp;V was notably lower (0.57 Ω) compared to that at OCV (1.05 Ω), suggesting that the electrode activation process was facilitated by the gradual penetration of the electrolyte and the appearance of metallic Mo. During the charging phase, the impedance exhibited an increasing trend, reaching 1.56 Ω in the fully charged state. This behavior demonstrates a reversible redox process characterized by superior kinetics. It was important to note that the impedance throughout the entire discharge-charge cycle remained below 2 Ω, and the impedance of the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> electrode was significantly lower than that of the MoSe<sub>2</sub> during all phases of the cycle (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31a</a>, Supporting Information), indicating that C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> had excellent conductivity, which was mainly attributed to the bandgap reduction caused by microcrystalline-amorphous heterointerface. Therefore, the charge self-regulation effect induced narrowing of the bandgap could reduce ohmic losses and accelerate the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion dynamics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0050_R_d87344890e2325" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Joule">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202405288-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/74c326bf-38a6-457f-88c8-9504027246dd/aenm202405288-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/74c326bf-38a6-457f-88c8-9504027246dd/aenm202405288-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/58035552-82bb-4e45-851e-63cde40816c4/aenm202405288-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/74c326bf-38a6-457f-88c8-9504027246dd/aenm202405288-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=aenm202405288-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Faenm.202405288" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) In situ galvanostatic electrochemical impedance spectra (GEIS) plots of C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> in the first cycle; b,c) DRT calculated from GEIS measurements at different voltage in discharge and charge process; d) 3D intensity color map of the contour DRT plots of the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>. The energy barriers of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion at e) crystalline structure; f) Amorphous structure; g) Microcrystalline-amorphous heterointerface. Insets show the diffusion path.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>To further explore the kinetic behavior of the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> electrode, we analyzed the DRT derived from the GEIS data using a Gaussian basis function. These DRT plots provided a model-free analysis of impedance variations, distinguishing between different interfacial electrochemical processes. The Nyquist plots from the frequency domain were transformed into time-domain DRT spectra through mathematical transformations (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32b</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0051_R_d87344890e2376" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Adv. Mater.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The x-axis represented the time constant (τ), calculated as the product of resistance (R) and capacitance (C),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0052_R_d87344890e2382" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - J. Phys.Chem. Lett.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which was independent of surface area and reflected the intrinsic properties of each process. The discharge/charge impedance spectra were interpreted using DRT functions presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0005">5b,c</a>. Four major peaks were identified across the timescales from 10<sup>−6</sup> to 0.5 × 10<sup>−4</sup> s (D1), 0.5 × 10<sup>−4</sup> to 10<sup>−3</sup> s (D2), 10<sup>−3</sup> to 10<sup>−1</sup> s (D3), and 10<sup>−1</sup> to 10 s (D4), each representing different aspects of electrochemical evolution. The D1 peaks correlated to the contact resistance (R<sub>s</sub>) between current collectors and active materials,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0053_R_d87344890e2408" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Mater. Today Energy">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> showed significant overlap and decreased markedly at the onset of discharge, stabilizing subsequently as illustrated in the intensity distribution graphs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0005">5d</a>). The D2 peaks, which were related to SEI production and ionic transport across the SEI (R<sub>SEI</sub>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0054_R_d87344890e2418" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - Adv. Mater.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> exhibited minimal changes, indicating the production of a uniform and thin SEI layer in the ether-based electrolyte, which underscored the stability of SEI in C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>. The D3 peaks corresponded to the charge transfer resistance (R<sub>ct</sub>) within the batteries, predominantly reflecting electrode interface reactions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0055_R_d87344890e2432" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Joule">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the R<sub>ct</sub> for C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> was significantly lower than that for MoSe<sub>2</sub> throughout the discharging/charging cycle, indicating enhanced interfacial charge transfer kinetics by the charge self-regulation effect. The D4 peaks represented diffusion impedance (W<sub>diff</sub>), with smaller peaks indicating more restricted diffusion. These peaks decreased during the discharge process as products partially clogged the electrode, a typical phenomenon in battery operation. Conversely, during the charging process, the D4 peaks increased, suggesting the decomposition of discharge products and the restoration of smoother diffusion.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0056_R_d87344890e2451" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Chem">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Remarkably, both the R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>ct</sub> were more stable in the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> electrode than in the MoSe<sub>2</sub>, as schemed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31b,c</a> (Supporting Information). This stability confirmed that the charge self-regulation effect generated by the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> structure could manipulate the electronic state at the electrode interface, accelerate the interfacial charge transfer kinetics, and contribute to the rapid transfer of Na<sup>+</sup>, thus forming a thin and stable SEI film on the electrode surface.</p>
            
            <p>We calculated the energy barriers for Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion across various pathways in different structural configurations, including crystalline structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0005">5e</a>), amorphous structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0005">5f</a>), and microcrystalline-amorphous heterointerface (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0005">5g</a>). The C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> electrode exhibited the lowest Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion barriers (0.32&nbsp;eV), compared with its crystalline (0.65&nbsp;eV) and amorphous (0.39&nbsp;eV) counterparts. The amorphous materials were long-range disordered structures, showing a random network arrangement and abundant isotropic ion diffusion channels, which will reduce the ion diffusion length. Therefore, the ionic diffusion barrier of the amorphous state was lower than that of the crystal.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0031_R_d87344890e2504" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Mater.">31</a>, <a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0057_R_d87344890e2504" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This indicated faster Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> electrode than in the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub> or A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> materials, consistent with the findings from GEIS and GITT (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0005">5a</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S34</a>, Supporting Information). These results confirmed that the charge self-regulation effect induced by the microcrystalline-amorphous heterointerface regulated the electron states at the heterointerface, reallocated the interfacial charge, enhanced facilitated electron/ion mobility, and improved the electrochemical reaction kinetics.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405288-sec-0090">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="aenm202405288-sec-0090-title">2.7 Electrochemical Characterizations of the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> <i>||</i> NVP Full Cell</h3>
            
            <p>To assess the practical application potential of C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> anode material in SIBs, we assembled a full cell using C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> anode and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>(NVP) cathode. The working mechanism of full cell is illustrated in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0006">6a</a>. The discharge and charge profiles for both half-cell and full-cell configurations were presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0006">6b</a>, displaying a distinct charge-discharge plateau ≈1.0−3.8&nbsp;V with a sloping feature. The cycling ability of the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>||NVP full cell was tested at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. The cell achieved a highly reversible capacity of 453.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with an ICE of 94.27%. After following 100 cycles, full cell still retained a capacity of 330.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a CE of 94.0% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0006">6c</a>). The initial three GCD curves of the full cell were observed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S37</a> (Supporting Information), clearly depicting the voltage plateau. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S38</a> (Supporting Information) showed the cycle performance of the full battery at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> high current density. After 50 cycles, full cell still retained a capacity of 314.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a CE of 98.5%, showing stable practical application potential. Additionally, the full cell demonstrated superior rate capabilities (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0006">6d</a>), delivering rate capacities of 511.6, 476.7, 427.5, 366.6, 261.6, 158.0, and 116.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5 and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Furthermore, the GCD curves from 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> to 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> were exhibited low polarization (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0006">6e</a>). It was verified that the full cell had excellent rate capability. The Ragone plot of the device was compared with reported results (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#aenm202405288-fig-0006">6f</a>), revealed that the full cell obtained an outstanding energy density of 352.4&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at power density of 59.1&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, and retained a energy density of 158.8&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at an ultrahigh power density of 6492.1&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>. These performance metrics were comparable to or surpass those reported full cell, demonstrating that the as-fabricated C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>||NVP system possessed excellent kinetics and superior stability, with potential for extensive applications (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0011_R_d87344890e2642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Nat. Commun.">11</a>, <a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0039_R_d87344890e2642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Mater.">39</a>, <a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0047_R_d87344890e2642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Mater.">47</a>, <a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0058_R_d87344890e2642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Adv. Energy Mater.">58</a>-<a href="#aenm202405288-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405288-bib-0063_R_d87344890e2642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Energy Storage Mater.">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="aenm202405288-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/8b012198-685f-4c11-a1cc-f49904a576ac/aenm202405288-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/8b012198-685f-4c11-a1cc-f49904a576ac/aenm202405288-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/fa0842f4-085c-4a42-84fb-0c1ad020b78a/aenm202405288-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/8b012198-685f-4c11-a1cc-f49904a576ac/aenm202405288-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">

                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic diagram of C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>||NVP full cell; b) Charge-discharge profiles of C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>, NVP, and full cell; c) Cycling performance of coin type full cell at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>; d) Rate capability of the full cell; e) GCD voltage profles of full cell at various rates; f) Comparison of the energy density of C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>||NVP full cell with the reported SIBs.</div>

            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202405288-sec-0100">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202405288-sec-0100-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we achieved ultrahigh-rate and robust sodium storage performance by constructing a microcrystalline-amorphous heterointerface network, designated as C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub>. In this work, the MoSe<sub>2</sub> microcrystalline regions acted as a supportive framework, while the amorphous MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> phase filled the interstitial gaps between the microcrystals. This electrode demonstrated a significant discharge capacity of 641.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at a current density of 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, surpassing the performance of its crystalline counterpart (MoSe<sub>2</sub>) and most reported anode materials for SIBs. Remarkably, the C-MoSe<sub>2</sub>/A-MoSe<sub>x</sub>O<sub>y</sub> electrode exhibited superior rate capabilities, maintaining a capacity of 324.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at high current density of 100 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Additionally, when assembled into a pouch cell, the electrode showcased an excellent energy density of 352.4&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>. This charge self-regulation effect induced by the microcrystalline-amorphous heterointerface activated the Mo─Se bond, further regulate the electron states at the heterointerface, causing charge redistribution at the heterogeneous interface, thereby reducing the charge transfer resistance, enhancing the kinetic properties of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion, and improving the electrochemical reversibility. The insights gained from the charge self-regulation effect in this microcrystalline-amorphous heterointerface network provided a compelling rationale for the design of high-rate electrodes in advanced energy storage applications.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
